title="Ice cap climate">EF</a></div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</b> is one of the most widely used <a href="/wiki/Climate_classification" title="Climate classification">climate classification</a> systems. It was first published by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_climate_scientists" title="List of climate scientists">climatologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Wladimir_K%C3%B6ppen" title="Wladimir K\xc3\xb6ppen">Wladimir K\xc3\xb6ppen</a> (1846-1940) in 1884,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> with several later modifications by K\xc3\xb6ppen, notably in 1918 and 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Later, the climatologist <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Geiger" title="Rudolf Geiger">Rudolf Geiger</a> (1954, 1961) introduced some changes to the classification system, which is thus sometimes called the <b>K\xc3\xb6ppen\xe2\x80\x93Geiger climate classification system.</b><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification divides climates into five main climate groups, with each group being divided based on seasonal precipitation and temperature patterns. The five main groups are <i>A</i> (tropical), <i>B</i> (dry), <i>C</i> (temperate), <i>D</i> (continental), and <i>E</i> (polar). Each group and subgroup is represented by a letter. All climates are assigned a main group (the first letter). All climates except for those in the <i>E</i> group are assigned a seasonal precipitation subgroup (the second letter). For example, <i>Af</i> indicates a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a>. The system assigns a temperature subgroup for all groups other than those in the <i>A</i> group, indicated by the third letter for climates in <i>B</i>, <i>C</i>, and <i>D</i>, and the second letter for climates in <i>E</i>. For example, <i>Cfb</i> indicates an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> with warm summers as indicated by the ending <i>b</i>. Climates are classified based on specific criteria unique to each climate type.<sup id="cite_ref-kottek2006_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottek2006-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>K\xc3\xb6ppen designed the system based on his experience as a <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">botanist</a>, so the main climate groups are based on the different variety of vegetation that grows in climates belonging to each group. In addition to identifying climates, the system can be used to analyze ecosystem conditions and identify the main types of vegetation within climates. Due to its link with the <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">plant life</a> of a region, the system is useful in predicting future changes in plant life within a region.\n</p><p>The K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification system has been further modified, within the <a href="/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification" title="Trewartha climate classification">Trewartha climate classification</a> system in the middle 1960s (revised in 1980). The Trewartha system sought to create a more refined middle <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> climate zone, which was one of the criticisms of the K\xc3\xb6ppen system (the C climate group was too broad).<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>200\xe2\x80\x931</span></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-9"><a href="#Mediterranean_climates"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Mediterranean climates</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10"><a href="#Humid_subtropical_climates"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Humid subtropical climates</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11"><a href="#Oceanic_climate"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Oceanic climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-12"><a href="#Highland_climates"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Highland climates</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Group_D:_Continental/microthermal_climates"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Group D: Continental/microthermal climates</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-14"><a href="#Hot_summer_continental_climates"><span class="tocnumber">2.4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Hot summer continental climates</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#Warm_summer_continental_or_hemiboreal_climates"><span class="tocnumber">2.4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Warm summer continental or hemiboreal climates</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#Subarctic_or_boreal_climates"><span class="tocnumber">2.4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Subarctic or boreal climates</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Group_E:_Polar_climates"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">Group E: Polar climates</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Ecological_significance"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Ecological significance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Trewartha_climate_classification_scheme"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Trewartha climate classification scheme</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Other_K\xc3\xb6ppen_climate_maps"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Other K\xc3\xb6ppen climate maps</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Climate_records"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Climate records</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meaning_of_symbols">Meaning of symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meaning of symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable floatright">\n<caption>K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification scheme symbols description table<sup id="cite_ref-Peel_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">1st\n</th>\n<th scope="col">2nd\n</th>\n<th scope="col">3rd\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" rowspan="4">A (Tropical)\n</th>\n<td>f (Rainforest)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>m (Monsoon)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>w (Savanna, Wet)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>s (Savanna, Dry)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" rowspan="5">B (Arid)\n</th>\n<td>W (Desert)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>S (Steppe)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>h (Hot)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>k (Cold)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>n (With frequent fog)<sup id="cite_ref-Cereceda_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cereceda-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" rowspan="6">C (Temperate)\n</th>\n<td>s (Dry summer)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>w (Dry winter)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>f (Without dry season)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>a (Hot summer)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>b (Warm summer)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>c (Cold summer)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" rowspan="7">D (Cold (continental))\n</th>\n<td>s (Dry summer)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>w (Dry winter)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>f (Without dry season)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>a (Hot summer)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>b (Warm summer)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>c (Cold summer)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td></td>\n<td>d (Very cold winter)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" rowspan="2">E (Polar)\n</th>\n<td>T (Tundra)</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>F (Eternal winter (ice cap))</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification scheme divides climates into five main climate groups: <i>A</i> (tropical), <i>B</i> (dry), <i>C</i> (temperate), <i>D</i> (continental), and <i>E</i> (polar).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The second letter indicates the seasonal precipitation type, while the third letter indicates the level of heat.<sup id="cite_ref-hanschen_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hanschen-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Group A: Tropical (megathermal) climates</b>\n</p><p>This type of climate has every month of the year with an average temperature of 18&#160;\xc2\xb0C (64.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) or higher, with significant precipitation.\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Af</i> = <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">Tropical rainforest climate</a>; average precipitation of at least 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in) in every month.</li>\n<li><i>Am</i> = <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">Tropical monsoon climate</a>; driest month (which nearly always occurs at or soon after the "winter" solstice for that side of the equator) with precipitation less than 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in), but more than 4% the total annual precipitation.</li>\n<li><i>Aw</i> or <i>As</i> = Tropical wet and dry or <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">savanna</a> climate; with the driest month having precipitation less than 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in) and less than 4% of the total annual precipitation.</li></ul>\n<p><b>Group B: Dry (arid and semiarid) climates</b>\n</p><p>This type of climate is defined by little precipitation.\n</p><p>Multiply the average annual temperature in <a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">Celsius</a> by 20, then add\n</p>\n<dl><dd>(a) 280 if 70% or more of the total precipitation is in the spring and summer months (April\xe2\x80\x93September in the Northern Hemisphere, or October\xe2\x80\x93March in the Southern), or</dd>\n<dd>(b) 140 if 30%\xe2\x80\x9370% of the total precipitation is received during the spring and summer, or</dd>\n<dd>(c) 0 if less than 30% of the total precipitation is received during the spring and summer.</dd></dl>\n<p>If the annual precipitation is less than 50% of this threshold, the classification is BW (arid: desert climate); if it is in the range of 50%\xe2\x80\x93100% of the threshold, the classification is BS (semi-arid: steppe climate).\n</p><p>A third letter can be included to indicate temperature. Originally, h signified low-latitude climate (average annual temperature above 18&#160;\xc2\xb0C (64.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F)) while k signified middle-latitude climate (average annual temperature below 18 \xc2\xb0C), but the more common practice today, especially in the United States, is to use h to mean the coldest month has an average temperature above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), with k denoting that at least one month\'s averages below 0 \xc2\xb0C (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)). The n is used to denote a climate characterized by frequent fog.<sup id="cite_ref-Cereceda_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cereceda-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gepchile_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepchile-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inzunza_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inzunza-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>BWh</i> = <a href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot desert climate">Hot desert climate</a></li>\n<li><i>BWk</i> = <a href="/wiki/Cold_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold desert climate">Cold desert climate</a></li>\n<li><i>BWn</i> = Desert climate with frequent fog<sup id="cite_ref-Cereceda_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cereceda-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gepchile_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepchile-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inzunza_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inzunza-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>BSh</i> = <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">Hot semi-arid climate</a></li>\n<li><i>BSk</i> = <a href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold semi-arid climate">Cold semi-arid climate</a></li>\n<li><i>BSn</i> = Semi-arid climate with frequent fog<sup id="cite_ref-Cereceda_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cereceda-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gepchile_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepchile-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inzunza_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inzunza-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p><b>Group C: Temperate (mesothermal) climates</b>\n</p><p>This type of climate has the coldest month averaging between 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)) and 18&#160;\xc2\xb0C (64.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and at least one month averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F).\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Cfa</i> = <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">Humid subtropical climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F)  (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), at least one month\'s average temperature above 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled). No dry months in the summer.</li>\n<li><i>Cfb</i> = Temperate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>\n<li><i>Cfc</i> = <a href="/wiki/Subpolar_oceanic_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subpolar oceanic climate">Subpolar oceanic climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F)  (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)) and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>\n<li><i>Cwa</i> = <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">Monsoon</a>-influenced humid subtropical climate; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F)  (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), at least one month\'s average temperature above 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>\n<li><i>Cwb</i> = <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_highland_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical highland climate">Subtropical highland climate</a> or Monsoon-influenced temperate oceanic climate; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (an alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation received in the warmest six months).</li>\n<li><i>Cwc</i> = Cold <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_highland_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical highland climate">subtropical highland climate</a> or Monsoon-influenced subpolar oceanic climate; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F)  (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)) and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>\n<li><i>Csa</i> = <a href="/wiki/Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot-summer Mediterranean climate">Hot-summer Mediterranean climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F)  (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), at least one month\'s average temperature above 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>\n<li><i>Csb</i> = <a href="/wiki/Warm-summer_Mediterranean_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Warm-summer Mediterranean climate">Warm-summer Mediterranean climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>\n<li><i>Csc</i> = <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cool-summer_Mediterranean_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cool-summer Mediterranean climate (page does not exist)">Cool-summer Mediterranean climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)) and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li></ul>\n<p><b>Group D: Continental (microthermal) climates</b>\n</p><p>This type of climate has at least one month averaging below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F))  and at least one month averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F).\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Dfa</i> = Hot-summer <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>; coldest month averaging below \xe2\x88\x920&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), at least one month\'s average temperature above 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>\n<li><i>Dfb</i> = Warm-summer <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>; coldest month averaging below \xe2\x88\x920&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>\n<li><i>Dfc</i> = <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">Subarctic climate</a>; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F))  and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>\n<li><i>Dfd</i> = Extremely cold subarctic climate; coldest month averaging below \xe2\x88\x9238&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9236.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>\n<li><i>Dwa</i> = Monsoon-influenced hot-summer humid continental climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), at least one month\'s average temperature above 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>\n<li><i>Dwb</i> = Monsoon-influenced warm-summer humid continental climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>\n<li><i>Dwc</i> = Monsoon-influenced <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a>; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F))  and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>\n<li><i>Dwd</i> = Monsoon-influenced extremely cold <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a>; coldest month averaging below \xe2\x88\x9238&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9236.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>\n<li><i>Dsa</i> = <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a>-influenced hot-summer humid continental climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), average temperature of the warmest month above 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>\n<li><i>Dsb</i> = Mediterranean-influenced warm-summer humid continental climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), average temperature of the warmest month below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>\n<li><i>Dsc</i> = subarctic climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F))  and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>\n<li><i>Dsd</i> = extremely cold, subarctic climate; coldest month averaging below \xe2\x88\x9238&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9236.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and 1\xe2\x80\x933 months averaging above 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li></ul>\n<p><b>Group E: Polar and alpine (montane) climates</b>\n</p><p>This type of climate has every month of the year with an average temperature below 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F).\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>ET</i> = <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">Tundra</a> climate; average temperature of warmest month between 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)) and 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F).</li>\n<li><i>EF</i> = <a href="/wiki/Ice_cap_climate" title="Ice cap climate">Ice cap climate</a>; eternal winter, with all 12 months of the year with average temperatures below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)).</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scheme">Scheme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Scheme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Group_A:_Tropical.2Fmegathermal_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_A:_Tropical/megathermal_climates">Group A: Tropical/megathermal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Group A: Tropical/megathermal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">Tropical climates</a> are characterized by constant high temperatures (at sea level and low elevations); all 12 months of the year have average temperatures of 18 \xc2\xb0C (64.4 \xc2\xb0F)  or higher. They are subdivided as follows:\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_rainforest_climate">Tropical rainforest climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tropical rainforest climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">Tropical rainforest climate</a></div>\n<p>All 12 months have an average precipitation of at least 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in). These climates usually occur within 10\xc2\xb0 latitude of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>.  This climate is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Doldrums" title="Doldrums">doldrums</a> low-pressure system all year round, so has no natural seasons in terms of thermal and moisture changes.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Apia" title="Apia">Apia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Balikpapan" title="Balikpapan">Balikpapan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Davao_City" title="Davao City">Davao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Guyana" title="Georgetown, Guyana">Georgetown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hilo,_Hawaii" title="Hilo, Hawaii">Hilo, Hawaii</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Innisfail,_Queensland" title="Innisfail, Queensland">Innisfail, Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kampala" title="Kampala">Kampala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kisumu,_Kenya" class="mw-redirect" title="Kisumu, Kenya">Kisumu, Kenya</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kuching" title="Kuching">Kuching</a>, Malaysia (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lae" title="Lae">Lae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Medan" title="Medan">Medan</a>, Indonesia (<i>Af</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Medell%C3%ADn" title="Medell\xc3\xadn">Medell\xc3\xadn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pontianak,_Indonesia" title="Pontianak, Indonesia">Pontianak</a>, Indonesia (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Quibd%C3%B3" title="Quibd\xc3\xb3">Quibd\xc3\xb3</a>, Colombia (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ratnapura" title="Ratnapura">Ratnapura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Salvador_da_Bahia" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvador da Bahia">Salvador da Bahia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santos,_Sao_Paulo" class="mw-redirect" title="Santos, Sao Paulo">Santos</a>, Brazil (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Suva" title="Suva">Suva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Toamasina" title="Toamasina">Toamasina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach, Florida</a>, United States (<i>Af</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<p>Some of the places with this climate are indeed uniformly and monotonously wet throughout the year (e.g., the northwest <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> coast of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> to <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>; see, for instance, <a href="/wiki/Andagoya" title="Andagoya">Andagoya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>), but in many cases, the period of higher sun and longer days is distinctly wettest (as at <a href="/wiki/Palembang" title="Palembang">Palembang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>) or the time of lower sun and shorter days may have more rain (as at <a href="/wiki/Sitiawan" title="Sitiawan">Sitiawan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>).\n</p><p>(<b>Note</b>. The term <a href="/wiki/Season" title="Season">aseasonal</a> refers to the lack in the tropical zone of large differences in daylight hours and mean monthly (or daily) temperature throughout the year. Annual cyclic changes occur in the tropics, but not as predictably as those in the temperate zone, albeit unrelated to temperature, but to water availability whether as rain, mist, soil, or ground water. Plant response (e. g., <a href="/wiki/Phenology" title="Phenology">phenology</a>), animal (feeding, migration, reproduction, etc.), and human activities (plant sowing, harvesting, hunting, fishing, etc.) are tuned to this \'seasonality\'. Indeed, in tropical South America and Central America, the \'rainy season\' (and the \'high water season\') is called <a href="/wiki/Rainy_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainy season"><i>invierno</i></a> or <i>inverno</i>, though it could occur in the Northern Hemisphere summer; likewise, the \'dry season\' (and \'low water season\') is called <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season"><i>verano</i></a> or <i>ver\xc3\xa3o</i>, and can occur in the Northern Hemisphere winter).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_monsoon_climate">Tropical monsoon climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tropical monsoon climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">Tropical monsoon climate</a></div>\n<p>This type of climate results from the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> winds which change direction according to the seasons. This climate has a driest month (which nearly always occurs at or soon after the "winter" solstice for that side of the equator) with rainfall less than 60 mm, but more than &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>25</sub></span> the total annual precipitation.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>208</span></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cairns" title="Cairns">Cairns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>Am</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chittagong,_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Chittagong, Bangladesh">Chittagong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coatzacoalcos" title="Coatzacoalcos">Coatzacoalcos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierre_Leone" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierre Leone">Sierre Leone</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guanare" title="Guanare">Guanare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hu%E1%BA%BF" title="Hu\xe1\xba\xbf">Hu\xe1\xba\xbf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Th%E1%BB%ABa_Thi%C3%AAn%E2%80%93Hu%E1%BA%BF_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Th\xe1\xbb\xaba Thi\xc3\xaan\xe2\x80\x93Hu\xe1\xba\xbf Province">Th\xe1\xbb\xaba Thi\xc3\xaan\xe2\x80\x93Hu\xe1\xba\xbf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kochi" title="Kochi">Kochi</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Libreville" title="Libreville">Libreville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9" title="Mal\xc3\xa9">Mal\xc3\xa9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Manaus" title="Manaus">Manaus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazonas_(Brazilian_state)" title="Amazonas (Brazilian state)">Amazonas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Port_Harcourt" title="Port Harcourt">Port Harcourt</a>, <a Ayacucho">Puerto Ayacucho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Qionghai_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Qionghai City">Qionghai City</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Taitung_City" title="Taitung City">Taitung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yangon" title="Yangon">Yangon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_wet_and_dry_or_savanna_climate">Tropical wet and dry or savanna climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical wet and dry or savanna climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">Tropical savanna climate</a></div>\n<p><i>Aw</i> climates have a pronounced dry season, with the driest month having precipitation less than 60 mm and less than &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>25</sub></span> of the total annual precipitation.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>208\xe2\x80\x9311</span></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a <i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, <a (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Mumbai" href="/wiki/Naples,_Florida" title="Naples, Florida">Naples</a>, Florida, United States (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Panama_City" title="Panama City">Panam\xc3\xa1 City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panam%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Panam\xc3\xa1">Panam\xc3\xa1</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ribeir%C3%A3o_Preto" title="Ribeir\xc3\xa3o Preto">Ribeir\xc3\xa3o Preto</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="S\xc3\xa3o Paulo (state)">S\xc3\xa3o Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, Brazil (<i>Aw</i>, bordering on <i>Am</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sanya" <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Veracruz,_Veracruz" class="mw-redirect" title="Veracruz, Veracruz">Veracruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a>, Mexico (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vientiane" title="Vientiane">Vientiane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaound\xc3\xa9">Yaound\xc3\xa9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> (<i>Aw</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<p>Most places that have this climate are found at the outer margins of the <a href="/wiki/Tropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical">tropical</a> zone from the low teens to the mid-20s latitudes, but occasionally an inner-tropical location (e.g., <a href="/wiki/San_Marcos,_Antioquia" title="San Marcos, Antioquia">San Marcos, Antioquia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>) also qualifies. Actually, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean sea">Caribbean</a> coast, eastward from the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Urab%C3%A1" title="Gulf of Urab\xc3\xa1">Gulf of Urab\xc3\xa1</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Panam%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Panam\xc3\xa1">Panam\xc3\xa1</a> border to the <a href="/wiki/Orinoco_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Orinoco River">Orinoco River</a> delta, on the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> (about 4,000 km), have long dry periods (the extreme is the <i>BSh</i> climate (see below), characterised by very low, unreliable precipitation, present, for instance, in extensive areas in the <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guajira_Pen%C3%ADnsula" class="extiw" title="es:Guajira Pen\xc3\xadnsula">Guajira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coro_region" title="Coro region">Coro</a>, western <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, the northernmost peninsulas in South America, which receive &lt;300 mm total annual precipitation, practically all in two or three months).\n</p><p>This condition extends to the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> forming the circum-Caribbean dry belt. The length and severity of the dry season diminishes inland (southward); at the latitude of the Amazon River\xe2\x80\x94which flows eastward, just south of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equatorial line</a>\xe2\x80\x94the climate is <i>Af</i>. East from the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a>, between the dry, arid Caribbean and the ever-wet Amazon are the Orinoco River\'s <a href="/wiki/Los_Llanos,_Venezuela" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Llanos, Venezuela">llanos</a> or <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, from where this climate takes its name.\n</p><p>Sometimes <i>As</i> is used in place of <i>Aw</i> if the dry season occurs during the time of higher sun and longer days. This is the case in parts of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, northwestern Dominican Republic, East Africa, and the Brazilian Northeastern Coast. In most places that have tropical wet and dry climates, however, the dry season occurs during the time of lower sun and shorter days because of <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> effects during the \'high-sun\' part of the year.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Monte_Cristi_(Dominican_Republic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Monte Cristi (Dominican Republic)">Monte Cristi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Recife,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Recife, Brazil">Recife</a>, Brazil (<i>As</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Natal,_Rio_Grande_do_Norte" title="Natal, Rio Grande do Norte">Natal</a>, Brazil (<i>As</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Trincomalee" title="Trincomalee">Trincomalee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> (<i>As</i>)</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Group_B:_Dry_.28desert_and_semi-arid.29_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_B:_Dry_(desert_and_semi-arid)_climates">Group B: Dry (desert and semi-arid) climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Group B: Dry (desert and semi-arid) climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">Desert climate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">Semi-arid climate</a></div>\n<p>These climates are characterized by actual precipitation less than a threshold value set equal to the <a href="/wiki/Potential_evapotranspiration" class="mw-redirect" title="Potential evapotranspiration">potential evapotranspiration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>212</span></sup> The threshold value (in millimeters) is determined as:\n</p><p>Multiply the average annual temperature in \xc2\xb0C by 20, then add (a) 280 if 70% or more of the total precipitation is in the high-sun half of the year (April through September in the Northern Hemisphere, or October through March in the Southern), or (b) 140 if 30%\xe2\x80\x9370% of the total precipitation is received during the applicable period, or (c) 0 if less than 30% of the total precipitation is so received.\n</p><p>According to the modified K\xc3\xb6ppen classification system used by modern climatologists, total precipitation in the warmest six months of the year is taken as reference instead of the total precipitation in the high-sun half of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>If the annual precipitation is less than 50% of this threshold, the classification is <i>BW</i> (arid: <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert climate</a>); if it is in the range of 50%\xe2\x80\x93100% of the threshold, the classification is <i>BS</i> (semi-arid: <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">steppe climate</a>).\n</p><p>A third letter can be included to indicate temperature. Originally, <i>h</i> signified low-latitude climate (average annual temperature above 18 \xc2\xb0C) while <i>k</i> signified middle-latitude climate (average annual temperature below 18 \xc2\xb0C), but the more common practice today, especially in the United States, is to use <i>h</i> to mean the coldest month has an average temperature above 0 \xc2\xb0C (32 \xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)), with <i>k</i> denoting that at least one month averages below 0 \xc2\xb0C.\n</p><p>Desert areas situated along the west coasts of continents at tropical or near-tropical locations are characterized by cooler temperatures than encountered elsewhere at comparable latitudes (due to the nearby presence of cold ocean currents) and frequent fog and low clouds, despite the fact that these places rank among the driest on earth in terms of actual precipitation received. This climate is sometimes labelled <i>BWn</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cereceda_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cereceda-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gepchile_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepchile-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inzunza_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inzunza-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The <i>BSn</i> category can be found in foggy coastal steppes.<sup id="cite_ref-Cereceda_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cereceda-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gepchile_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepchile-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inzunza_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inzunza-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Desert climate examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; (<i>BWh</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Almer%C3%ADa" title="Almer\xc3\xada">Almer\xc3\xada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (<i>BWh</i>, bordering on <i>BSh</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> (<i>BWh</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Upington" (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ulan-Ude" title="Ulan-Ude">Ulan-Ude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lethbridge,_Alberta" class="mw-redirect" title="Lethbridge, Alberta">Lethbridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brooks,_Alberta" title="Brooks, Alberta">Brooks</a>, Alberta, Canada (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aleppo" title="Aleppo">Aleppo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Shijiazhuang" title="Shijiazhuang">Shijiazhuang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a>, China (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lhasa" title="Lhasa">Lhasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibet_Autonomous_Region" title="Tibet Autonomous Region">Tibet Autonomous Region</a>, China (<i>BSk</i> bordering on <i>Dwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ulaanbaatar" Rivadavia">Comodoro Rivadavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Quiaca" title="La Quiaca">La Quiaca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jujuy_Province" title="Jujuy Province">Jujuy</a>, Argentina (<i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/L%27Agulhas" title="L&#39;Agulhas">L\'Agulhas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Cape" title="Western Cape">Western Cape</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> (<i>BSn</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sana%27a" title="Sana&#39;a">Sana\'a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> (<i>BSk</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<p>On occasion, a fourth letter is added to indicate if either the winter or summer half of the year is "wetter" than the other half. To qualify, the wettest month must have at least 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in) of average precipitation if all 12 months are above 18 \xc2\xb0C (64 \xc2\xb0F), or 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in) if not; plus at least 70% of the total precipitation must be in the same half of the year as the wettest month \xe2\x80\x94 but the letter used indicates when the \'dry\' season occurs, not the \'wet\' one. This would result in <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a>, Sudan, being reckoned as <i>BWhw</i>; <a href="/wiki/Niamey" title="Niamey">Niamey</a>, Niger, as <i>BShw</i>; <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, Egypt, as <i>BWhs</i>; <a href="/wiki/Asbi%27ah" class="mw-redirect" title="Asbi&#39;ah">Asbi\'ah</a>, Libya, as <i>BShs</i>; <a href="/wiki/%C3%96mn%C3%B6govi_Province" title="\xc3\x96mn\xc3\xb6govi Province">\xc3\x96mn\xc3\xb6govi Province</a>, Mongolia, as <i>BWkw</i>; and <a href="/wiki/Xining" title="Xining">Xining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qinghai" title="Qinghai">Qinghai</a>, China, as <i>BSkw</i> (<i>BWks</i> and <i>BSks</i> do not exist if 0 \xc2\xb0C in the coldest month is recognized as the <i>h</i>/<i>k</i> boundary.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>) If the standards for neither <i>w</i> nor <i>s</i> are met, no fourth letter is added.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Group_C:_Temperate.2Fmesothermal_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_C:_Temperate/mesothermal_climates">Group C: Temperate/mesothermal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Group C: Temperate/mesothermal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><span id="Group_C"></span>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">Temperate climate</a></div>\n<p>In the Koppen climate system, temperate climates are defined as having an average temperature above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (26.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), as noted previously) in their coldest month but below 18&#160;\xc2\xb0C (64.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F). The average temperature of \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (26.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) roughly coincides with the equatorward limit of frozen ground and snowcover lasting for a month or more.\n</p><p>The second letter indicates the precipitation pattern\xe2\x80\x94<i>w</i> indicates dry winters (driest winter month average precipitation less than one-tenth wettest summer month average precipitation. <i>s</i> indicates at least three times as much rain in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer. <i>f</i> means significant precipitation in all seasons (neither above-mentioned set of conditions fulfilled).<sup id="cite_ref-Peel_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The third letter indicates the degree of summer heat\xe2\x80\x94<i>a</i> indicates warmest month average temperature above 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) while  <i>b</i> indicates warmest month averaging below 22 \xc2\xb0C.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mediterranean_climates">Mediterranean climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mediterranean climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a></div>\n<p>These climates usually occur on the western sides of continents between the latitudes of 30\xc2\xb0 and 45\xc2\xb0.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> These climates are in the polar front region in winter, and thus have moderate temperatures and changeable, rainy weather. Summers are hot and dry, due to the domination of the subtropical high pressure systems, except in the immediate coastal areas, where summers are milder due to the nearby presence of cold ocean currents that may bring <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">fog</a> but prevent rain.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>221\xe2\x80\x933</span></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Latakia" title="Latakia">Latakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Halabja" title="Halabja">Halabja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, Israel (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Naples">Naples</a>, Italy (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Faro,_Portugal" title="Faro, Portugal">Faro</a>, Portugal (<i>Csa</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nice,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Nice, France">Nice</a>, France (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> (<i>Csa</i> bordering on <i>BSh</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Antalya" title="Antalya">Antalya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Izmir" class="mw-redirect" title="Izmir">Izmir</a>, Turkey (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dushanbe" title="Dushanbe">Dushanbe</a>, <a Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" California">Sacramento</a>, California, United States (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Medford,_Oregon" title="Medford, Oregon">Medford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, United States (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>Csa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>, Australia (<i>Csa</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<p>Dry-summer climates sometimes extend to additional areas (sometimes well north,  or south of) typical Mediterranean climates, however the warmest month mean does not reach 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) they are classified as (<i>Csb</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Peel_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Some of these areas would border the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate</a> (<i>Cfb</i>), except their dry-summer patterns meet K\xc3\xb6ppen\'s <i>Cs</i> minimum thresholds.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> (<i>Csb</i> bordering <i>BSk</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="A Coru\xc3\xb1a">A Coru\xc3\xb1a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (<i>Csb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Essaouira" title="Essaouira">Essaouira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> (<i>Csb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> (<i>Csb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Potenza,_Italy" class="mw-redirect" title="Potenza, Italy">Potenza</a>, Italy (<i>Csb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco</a>, California, United States (<i>Csb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California" title="Santa Barbara, California">Santa Barbara</a>, California, United States (<i>Csb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (<i>Csb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> (<i>Csb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Albany,_Western_Australia" title="Albany, Western Australia">Albany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>, Australia (<i>Csb</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>Cold-summer Mediterranean climates (<i>Csc</i>) exist in high-elevation areas adjacent to coastal <i>Csb</i> climate areas, where the strong maritime influence prevents the average winter monthly temperature from dropping below 0 \xc2\xb0C. This climate is rare and is predominantly found in climate fringes and isolated areas of the Cascades and Andes Mountains, as the dry-summer climate extends further poleward in the Americas than elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Rare instances of this climate can be found in some coastal locations in the North Atlantic and at high altitudes in Hawaii.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Balmaceda,_Chile" title="Balmaceda, Chile">Balmaceda</a>, Chile (<i>Csc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Haleakal%C4%81" title="Haleakal\xc4\x81">Haleakal\xc4\x81 Summit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, United States (<i>Csc</i>)</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Humid_subtropical_climates">Humid subtropical climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Humid subtropical climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">Humid subtropical climate</a></div>\n<p>These climates usually occur on the eastern coasts and eastern sides of continents, usually in the high 20s and 30s latitudes. Unlike the dry summer Mediterranean climates, humid subtropical climates have a warm and wet flow from the tropics that creates warm and moist conditions in the summer months. As such, summer (not winter as is the case in Mediterranean climates) is often the wettest season.\n</p><p>The flow out of the subtropical highs and the summer monsoon creates a southerly flow from the tropics that brings warm and moist air to the lower east sides of continents. This flow is often what brings the frequent but short-lived summer thundershowers so typical of the more southerly subtropical  climates like the far southern United States, southern China and Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>223\xe2\x80\x936</span></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Montevideo" title="Montevideo">Montevideo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunci\xc3\xb3n">Asunci\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a> (<i>Cfa</i>, bordering on <i>Aw</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">Campinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Albury" title="Albury">Albury</a>, Australia (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Washington_DC" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington DC">Washington DC</a>, <a United States (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Astara,_Azerbaijan" title="Astara, Azerbaijan">Astara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Belgrade,_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgrade, Serbia">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> (<i>Cfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a title="South Africa">South Africa</a> (<i>Cfa</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<p>Subtropical-Dry Winter (<i>Cwa</i>) is monsoonal influenced, having the classic dry winter/wet summer pattern associated with tropical monsoonal climates.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" (<i>Cwa</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceanic_climate">Oceanic climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Oceanic climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate</a></div>\n<p><i>Cfb</i> climates usually occur in the higher middle latitudes on the western sides of continents between the latitudes of 40\xc2\xb0 and 60\xc2\xb0; they are typically situated immediately poleward of the Mediterranean climates, although in Australia and extreme southern Africa this climate is found immediately poleward of temperate climates, and at a somewhat lower latitude. In western Europe, this climate occurs in coastal areas up to 63\xc2\xb0N in Norway.\n</p><p>These climates are dominated all year round by the polar front, leading to changeable, often overcast weather. Summers are mild due to cool ocean currents, although hotter, stable weather patterns can set in for periods of time, typically longer at the lower latitude range in the northern hemisphere. Winters are milder than other climates in similar latitudes, but usually very cloudy however not always wet. <i>Cfb</i> climates are also encountered at high elevations in certain subtropical and tropical areas, where the climate would be that of a subtropical/tropical rain forest if not for the altitude. These climates are called "highlands".<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>226\xe2\x80\x939</span></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mar_del_Plata" title="Mar del Plata">Mar del Plata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Province" title="Buenos Aires Province">Buenos Aires Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina"
