Region</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<p>Subpolar oceanic climates (<i>Cfc</i>) occur poleward of or at higher elevations than the maritime temperate climates, and are mostly confined either to narrow coastal strips on the western poleward margins of the continents, or, especially in the Northern Hemisphere, to islands off such coasts. They occur in both hemispheres, most often at latitudes from 60\xc2\xb0 north and south to 70\xc2\xb0 north and south.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk">Reykjav\xc3\xadk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> (<i>Cfc</i>, borders on <i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/T%C3%B3rshavn" title="T\xc3\xb3rshavn">T\xc3\xb3rshavn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%B8st" title="R\xc3\xb8st">R\xc3\xb8st</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Read_(Tasmania)" title="Mount Read (Tasmania)">Mount Read</a>, Tasmania, Australia (<i>Cfc</i>, borders on ET)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Auckland_Islands" title="Auckland Islands">Auckland Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Punta_Arenas" title="Punta Arenas">Punta Arenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Unalaska,_Alaska" title="Unalaska, Alaska">Unalaska</a>, Alaska, United States (<i>Cfc</i>)</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Highland_climates">Highland climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Highland climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Dry-winter highland climate (<i>Cwb</i>) is a type of climate mainly found in highlands inside the tropics of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> or central Argentina and areas outside of the tropics (such as in the subtropics). Winters are noticeable and dry, and summers can be very rainy. In the tropics, the rainy season is provoked by the tropical air masses and the dry winters by subtropical high pressure.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Da_Lat" title="Da Lat">Da Lat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Shimla" title="Shimla">Shimla</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thimphu" title="Thimphu">Thimphu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mokhotlong" title="Mokhotlong">Mokhotlong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mbabane" title="Mbabane">Mbabane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Swaziland">Swaziland</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baguio" title="Baguio">Baguio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kunming" title="Kunming">Kunming</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Harare" title="Harare">Harare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Antananarivo" title="Antananarivo">Antananarivo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cusco" title="Cusco">Cusco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> (<i>Cwb</i> bordering on <i>Cwc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Salta" title="Salta">Salta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>Highland climates with uniform rainfall (<i>Cfb</i>) are a type of oceanic climate mainly found in highlands of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, such as in or around the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dividing_Range" title="Great Dividing Range">Great Dividing Range</a> in the states of <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria (state)">Victoria</a>, and also sparsely in other continents, such as in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, among others. Unlike a typical <i>Cwb</i> climate, they tend to have rainfall spread evenly throughout the year. They have characteristics of both the <i>Cfb</i> and <i>Cfa</i> climates. Though unlike these climates, they have a high <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">diurnal temperature variation</a> and low humidity, owing to their inland location and relatively high <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">elevation</a>.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Province" title="Pichincha Province">Pichincha Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogot\xc3\xa1">Bogot\xc3\xa1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department" title="Cundinamarca Department">Cundinamarca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">Curitiba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paran\xc3\xa1 (state)">Paran\xc3\xa1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Campos_do_Jord%C3%A3o" title="Campos do Jord\xc3\xa3o">Campos do Jord\xc3\xa3o</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="S\xc3\xa3o Paulo (state)">S\xc3\xa3o Paulo</a>, Brazil (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Boone,_North_Carolina" title="Boone, North Carolina">Boone</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, United States (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Constanza,_Dominican_Republic" title="Constanza, Dominican Republic">Constanza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bathurst,_New_South_Wales" title="Bathurst, New South Wales">Bathurst</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Orange,_New_South_Wales" title="Orange, New South Wales">Orange</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cameron_Highlands_District" title="Cameron Highlands District">Cameron Highlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nuwara_Eliya" title="Nuwara Eliya">Nuwara Eliya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mendi" title="Mendi">Mendi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Hagen" title="Mount Hagen">Mount Hagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> (<i>Cfb</i>)</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Group_D:_Continental.2Fmicrothermal_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_D:_Continental/microthermal_climates">Group D: Continental/microthermal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Group D: Continental/microthermal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">Continental climate</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG/220px-Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG/330px-Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG/440px-Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2260" data-file-height="3390" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The snowy city of <a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a></div></div></div>\n<p>These climates have an average temperature above 10 \xc2\xb0C (50 \xc2\xb0F) in their warmest months, and a coldest month average below 0 \xc2\xb0C (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F), as noted previously). These usually occur in the interiors of continents and on their upper east coasts, normally north of 40\xc2\xb0N. In the Southern Hemisphere, group D climates are extremely rare due to the smaller land masses in the middle latitudes and the almost complete absence of land at 40\xe2\x80\x9360\xc2\xb0S, existing only in some highland locations.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hot_summer_continental_climates">Hot summer continental climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hot summer continental climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hot-summer_humid_continental_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot-summer humid continental climate">Hot-summer humid continental climate</a></div>\n<p><i>Dfa</i> climates usually occur in the high 30s and low 40s latitudes, with a qualifying average temperature in the warmest month of greater than 22 \xc2\xb0C/72 \xc2\xb0F. In Europe, these climates tend to be much drier than in North America. In eastern Asia, <i>Dwa</i> climates extend further south due to the influence of the Siberian high pressure system, which also causes winters there to be dry, and summers can be very wet because of <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> circulation. <i>Dsa</i> exists at higher elevations adjacent to areas with hot summer Mediterranean (<i>Csa</i>) climates.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>231\xe2\x80\x932</span></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Oral,_Kazakhstan" title="Oral, Kazakhstan">Oral</a>, Kazakhstan (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aomori,_Aomori" class="mw-redirect" title="Aomori, Aomori">Aomori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aomori_Prefecture" title="Aomori Prefecture">Aomori Prefecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nagano,_Nagano" class="mw-redirect" title="Nagano, Nagano">Nagano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagano_Prefecture" title="Nagano Prefecture">Nagano Prefecture</a>, Japan (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a>, Japan (<i>Dfa</i>, bordering on <i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, United States (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, United States (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>, United States (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, Canada (<i>Dfa</i>, bordering on <i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, Canada (<i>Dfa</i>, bordering on <i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Ontario" title="Windsor, Ontario">Windsor</a>, Ontario, Canada (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rostov-on-Don" title="Rostov-on-Don">Rostov-on-Don</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Volgograd" title="Volgograd">Volgograd</a>, Russia (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pyongyang" title="Pyongyang">Pyongyang</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> (<i>Dwa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (<i>Dwa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (<i>Dwa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Harbin" title="Harbin">Harbin</a>, China (<i>Dwa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a>, China (<i>Dwa</i>)</li></ul>\n<p><i>Dsa</i> exists only at higher elevations adjacent to areas with hot summer Mediterranean (<i>Csa</i>) climates.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saqqez" title="Saqqez">Saqqez</a>, Kurdistan Province, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arak,_Iran" title="Arak, Iran">Arak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Markazi_Province" title="Markazi Province">Markazi Province</a>, Iran (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hakk%C3%A2ri" title="Hakk\xc3\xa2ri">Hakk\xc3\xa2ri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mu%C5%9F" title="Mu\xc5\x9f">Mu\xc5\x9f</a>, Turkey (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Idaho" title="Cambridge, Idaho">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a>, United States (<i>Dsa</i>)</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Warm_summer_continental_or_hemiboreal_climates">Warm summer continental or hemiboreal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Warm summer continental or hemiboreal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Warm-summer_humid_continental_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Warm-summer humid continental climate">Warm-summer humid continental climate</a></div>\n<p><i>Dfb</i> and <i>Dwb</i> climates are immediately poleward of hot summer continental climates, generally in the high 40s and low 50s latitudes in North America and Asia, and also extending to higher latitudes in central and eastern Europe and Russia, between the maritime temperate and continental subarctic climates, where it extends up to 65 degrees latitude in places.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kushiro,_Hokkaido" title="Kushiro, Hokkaido">Kushiro, Hokkaido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Karaganda" title="Karaganda">Karaganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tallinn" <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Moscow,_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow, Russia">Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a Petersburg</a>, Russia (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Warsaw" href="/wiki/Pristina,_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Pristina, Kosovo">Pristina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Erzurum" title="Erzurum">Erzurum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ardahan" title="Ardahan">Ardahan</a>, Turkey (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (<i>Dfb/Dwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, United States (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>\n<li><a (<i>Dwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a>, Russia (<i>Dwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baruunturuun" title="Baruunturuun">Baruunturuun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> (<i>Dwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pyeongchang_County" title="Pyeongchang County">Pyeongchang County</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (<i>Dwb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Rushmore,_South_Dakota" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Rushmore, South Dakota">Mount Rushmore</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a>, United States (<i>Dwb</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<p><i>Dsb</i> arises from the same scenario as <i>Dsa</i>, but at even higher altitudes or latitudes, and chiefly in North America, since the Mediterranean climates extend further poleward than in Eurasia.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Sivas" title="Sivas">Sivas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turke" class="mw-redirect" title="Turke">Turkey</a> (<i>Dsb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roghun" title="Roghun">Roghun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> (<i>Dsb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dras" title="Dras">Dras</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (<i>Dsb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Flagstaff,_Arizona" title="Flagstaff, Arizona">Flagstaff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, United States (<i>Dsb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_Lake_Tahoe,_California" title="South Lake Tahoe, California">South Lake Tahoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, United States (<i>Dsb</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wallace,_Idaho" title="Wallace, Idaho">Wallace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a>, United States (<i>Dsb</i>)</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Subarctic_or_boreal_climates">Subarctic or boreal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Subarctic or boreal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">Subarctic climate</a></div>\n<p><i>Dfc</i>, <i>Dsc</i> and <i>Dwc</i> climates occur poleward of the other group D climates, generally in the 50 and low 60 degrees of North latitude. In some places, it extends northward to beyond 70\xc2\xb0N latitude.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>232\xe2\x80\x935</span></sup>\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>:\n</p>\n<div>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yellowknife" title="Yellowknife">Yellowknife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>, Canada (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Whitehorse,_Yukon" title="Whitehorse, Yukon">Whitehorse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a>, Canada (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Labrador_City" title="Labrador City">Labrador City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, Canada (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anchorage,_Alaska" title="Anchorage, Alaska">Anchorage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, United States (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fairbanks,_Alaska" title="Fairbanks, Alaska">Fairbanks</a>, Alaska, United States (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fraser,_Colorado" title="Fraser, Colorado">Fraser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, United States (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Buller,_Victoria" title="Mount Buller, Victoria">Mount Buller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>, Australia (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Pass,_New_South_Wales" title="Charlotte Pass, New South Wales">Charlotte Pass</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, Australia (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Murmansk" title="Murmansk">Murmansk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murmansk_Oblast" title="Murmansk Oblast">Murmansk Oblast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk" title="Arkhangelsk">Arkhangelsk</a>, Russia (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aldan,_Russia" title="Aldan, Russia">Aldan</a>, Russia (<i>Dfc</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Troms%C3%B8" title="Troms\xc3\xb8">Troms\xc3\xb8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St._Moritz" title="St. Moritz">St. Moritz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grisons" class="mw-redirect" title="Grisons">Grisons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kangerlussuaq" title="Kangerlussuaq">Kangerlussuaq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Homer,_Alaska" title="Homer, Alaska">Homer</a>, Alaska, United States (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bodie,_California" title="Bodie, California">Bodie</a>, California, United States (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brian_Head,_Utah" title="Brian Head, Utah">Brian Head</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, United States (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anadyr" class="mw-disambig" title="Anadyr">Anadyr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mohe_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohe County">Mohe County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heilongjiang" title="Heilongjiang">Heilongjiang</a>, China (<i>Dwc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yushu_City,_Qinghai" title="Yushu City, Qinghai">Yushu City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qinghai" title="Qinghai">Qinghai</a>, China (<i>Dwc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6r%C3%B6n" title="M\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb6n">M\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb6n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> (<i>Dwc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lukla" title="Lukla">Lukla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> (<i>Dwc</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</div>\n<p>Places with this climate (<i>Dfd</i>, <i>Dwd</i>, <i>Dsd</i>) have severe winters, with the temperature in their coldest month lower than \xe2\x88\x9238 \xc2\xb0C. These climates occur only in eastern <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. The names of some of the places with this climate have become veritable synonyms for extreme, severe winter cold.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">Yakutsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sakha_Republic" title="Sakha Republic">Sakha Republic</a>, Russia (<i>Dfd</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Verkhoyansk" title="Verkhoyansk">Verkhoyansk</a>, Sakha Republic, Russia (<i>Dfd</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Amga_(rural_locality)" title="Amga (rural locality)">Amga</a>, Sakha Republic, Russia (<i>Dfd</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Oymyakon" title="Oymyakon">Oymyakon</a>, Sakha Republic, Russia (<i>Dwd</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Seymchan_(urban-type_settlement)" title="Seymchan (urban-type settlement)">Seymchan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magadan_Oblast" title="Magadan Oblast">Magadan Oblast</a>, Russia (<i>Dwd</i>)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_E:_Polar_climates">Group E: Polar climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Group E: Polar climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the K\xc3\xb6ppen climate system, polar climates are defined as the warmest temperature of any month is below 10 \xc2\xb0C (50 \xc2\xb0F). Polar climates are further divided into two types, tundra climates and icecap climates:\n</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">Tundra</a> climate</b> (<i>ET</i> and <i>ETf</i>): Warmest month has an average temperature between 0 and 10 \xc2\xb0C. These climates occur on the northern edges of the North American and Eurasian land masses (generally north of 70 \xc2\xb0N although it may be found farther south depending on local conditions), and on nearby islands. <i>ET</i> climates are also found on some islands near the Antarctic Convergence, and at high elevations outside the polar regions, above the tree line.\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Rainier,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Rainier, Washington">Mount Rainier</a>, Washington, United States (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Island" title="Macquarie Island">Macquarie Island</a>, Australia (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Crozet_Islands" title="Crozet Islands">Crozet Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Campbell_Island,_New_Zealand" title="Campbell Island, New Zealand">Campbell Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kerguelen_Islands" title="Kerguelen Islands">Kerguelen Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Edwards_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Edwards Islands">Prince Edwards Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stanley,_Falkland_Islands" title="Stanley, Falkland Islands">Stanley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>), borders subpolar oceanic (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ushuaia" title="Ushuaia">Ushuaia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> (<i>ET</i>), (borders on <i>Cfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Wellington_(Tasmania)" title="Mount Wellington (Tasmania)">Mount Wellington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nagqu" title="Nagqu">Nagqu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>, China (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Letseng_diamond_mine" title="Letseng diamond mine">Letseng diamond mine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a> (<i>ET</i>, bordering on <i>Cfc</i> and <i>Dfc</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Rinconada,_Peru" title="La Rinconada, Peru">La Rinconada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cairn_Gorm" title="Cairn Gorm">Cairn Gorm</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>These climates are a colder and more continental variants of tundra. They would have characteristics of the ice cap climate, but still manage to see monthly average temperatures above 0 \xc2\xb0C (32 \xc2\xb0F):\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Nanortalik" title="Nanortalik">Nanortalik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Fuji" title="Mount Fuji">Mount Fuji</a>, Japan (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Murghab,_Tajikistan" title="Murghab, Tajikistan">Murghab, Tajikistan</a> (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington,_New_Hampshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Washington, New Hampshire">Mount Washington</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, United States (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Zugspitze" title="Zugspitze">Zugspitze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eureka,_Nunavut" title="Eureka, Nunavut">Eureka, Nunavut</a>, Canada (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Iqaluit,_Nunavut" class="mw-redirect" title="Iqaluit, Nunavut">Iqaluit, Nunavut</a>, Canada (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inukjuak,_Quebec" class="mw-redirect" title="Inukjuak, Quebec">Inukjuak, Quebec</a>, Canada (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nuuk,_Greenland" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuuk, Greenland">Nuuk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (<i>ETf</i>, bordering on Dfc)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Svalbard" title="Svalbard">Svalbard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mys_Shmidta" title="Mys Shmidta">Mys Shmidta</a>, Russia (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dikson_Island" title="Dikson Island">Dikson Island</a>, Russia (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nord,_Greenland" title="Nord, Greenland">Nord</a>, Greenland (<i>ETf</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Esperanza_Base" title="Esperanza Base">Esperanza Base</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> (<i>ETf</i>)</li></ul>\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/Ice_cap_climate" title="Ice cap climate">Ice cap climate</a></b> (<i>EF</i>): This climate is dominant in Antarctica and inner Greenland, but also occurs at extremely high altitudes on mountains, above even tundra. Monthly average temperatures never exceed 0 \xc2\xb0C (32 \xc2\xb0F) ((or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)).\n</p><p><b>Examples</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Mount Ararat</a>, Turkey (<i>EF</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Grossglockner" title="Grossglockner">Grossglockner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carinthia" title="Carinthia">Carinthia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> (<i>EF</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a>, China/Nepal (<i>EF</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Summit_Camp" title="Summit Camp">Summit Camp</a>, Greenland (<i>EF</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scott_Base" title="Scott Base">Scott Base</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> (<i>EF</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vostok_Station" title="Vostok Station">Vostok Station</a>, Antarctica (<i>EF</i>), location of the lowest air temperature ever recorded on Earth.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/McMurdo_Station" title="McMurdo Station">McMurdo Station</a>, Antarctica (<i>EF</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Byrd_Station" title="Byrd Station">Byrd Station</a>, Antarctica (<i>EF</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>Occasionally, a third, lower-case letter is added to ET climates (distinguishing between ETf, ETs, and ETw), if either the summer or winter is clearly drier than the other half of the year. When the option to include this letter is exercised, the same standards that are used for Groups C and D apply, with the additional requirement that the wettest month must have an average of at least 30 mm precipitation (Group E climates can be as dry or even drier than Group B climates based on actual precipitation received, but their rate of evaporation is much lower). Seasonal precipitation letters are almost never attached to EF climates, mainly due to the difficulty in distinguishing between falling and blowing snow, as snow is the sole source of moisture in these climates.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_significance">Ecological significance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ecological significance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification is based on the empirical relationship between climate and vegetation. This classification provides an efficient way to describe climatic conditions defined by temperature and precipitation and their seasonality with a single metric. Because climatic conditions identified by the K\xc3\xb6ppen classification are ecologically relevant, it has been widely used to map geographic distribution of long term climate and associated ecosystem conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Chen_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chen-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Over the recent years, there has been an increasing interest in using the classification to identify changes in climate and potential changes in vegetation over time.<sup id="cite_ref-hanschen_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hanschen-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The most important ecological significance of the K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification is that it helps to predict the dominant vegetation type based on the climatic data and vice versa.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, a <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_University" title="Nanjing University">Nanjing University</a> paper published in <i><a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">Nature</a></i> analyzing climate classifications found that between 1950 and 2010, approximately 5.7% of all land area worldwide had moved from wetter and colder classifications to drier and hotter classifications. The authors also found that the change "cannot be explained as natural variations but are driven by anthropogenic factors."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trewartha_climate_classification_scheme">Trewartha climate classification scheme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Trewartha climate classification scheme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(March 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification" title="Trewartha climate classification">Trewartha climate classification</a></div>\n<p>The Trewartha climate classification is a climate classification system published by American geographer Glenn Thomas Trewartha in 1966, and updated in 1980. It is a modified version of the 1899 K\xc3\xb6ppen system, created to answer some of the deficiencies of the K\xc3\xb6ppen system. The Trewartha system attempts to redefine the middle latitudes to be closer to vegetation zoning and genetic climate systems. It was considered a more true or "real world" reflection of the global climate.\n</p><p>For example, under the standard K\xc3\xb6ppen system, in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, western <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a> are classed into the same climate zone as <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">southern California</a>, even though the two regions have strikingly different weather and vegetation. Under the old K\xc3\xb6ppen system cool oceanic climates like that of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> or <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> were classed in the same zone as hot subtropical cities like <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah, Georgia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Brisbane,_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Brisbane, Australia">Brisbane, Australia</a>. In the United States, locations like <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a> which have long, severe winter climates where plants are completely dormant, were classed into the same climate zone as <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> or northern <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> which have mild winters and a green winter landscape.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Other_K.C3.B6ppen_climate_maps"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_K\xc3\xb6ppen_climate_maps">Other K\xc3\xb6ppen climate maps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Other K\xc3\xb6ppen climate maps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>All maps use the \xe2\x89\xa50 \xc2\xb0C definition for temperate climates and the 18 \xc2\xb0C annual mean temperature threshold to distinguish between hot and cold dry climates.<sup id="cite_ref-Peel_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" style="text-align:center">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1425" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>North America\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: data-file-height="1900" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Europe\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 152px"><div style="width:
